  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_347d9bb5-a48a-47e9-917f-26aa5de93d4c'

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer8008518370264116990"><b>From <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author Julia Quinn comes the first novel in the beloved Regency-set world of her charming, powerful Bridgerton family, now a series created by Shonda Rhimes for Netflix.</b><br/><br/>In the ballrooms and drawing rooms of Regency London, rules abound. From their earliest days, children of aristocrats learn how to address an earl and curtsey before a prince</span>
  <span id="freeText8008518370264116990" style="display:none"><b>From <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author Julia Quinn comes the first novel in the beloved Regency-set world of her charming, powerful Bridgerton family, now a series created by Shonda Rhimes for Netflix.</b><br /><br />In the ballrooms and drawing rooms of Regency London, rules abound. From their earliest days, children of aristocrats learn how to address an earl and curtsey before a prince—while other dictates of the ton are unspoken yet universally understood. A proper duke should be imperious and aloof. A young, marriageable lady should be amiable…but not too amiable.<br /><br />Daphne Bridgerton has always failed at the latter. The fourth of eight siblings in her close-knit family, she has formed friendships with the most eligible young men in London. Everyone likes Daphne for her kindness and wit. But no one truly desires her. She is simply too deuced honest for that, too unwilling to play the romantic games that captivate gentlemen.<br /><br />Amiability is not a characteristic shared by Simon Basset, Duke of Hastings. Recently returned to England from abroad, he intends to shun both marriage and society—just as his callous father shunned Simon throughout his painful childhood. Yet an encounter with his best friend’s sister offers another option. If Daphne agrees to a fake courtship, Simon can deter the mamas who parade their daughters before him. Daphne, meanwhile, will see her prospects and her reputation soar.<br /><br />The plan works like a charm—at first. But amid the glittering, gossipy, cut-throat world of London’s elite, there is only one certainty: love ignores every rule...</span>
  <a data-text-id="8008518370264116990" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13715563213382984385"><i>This review is dedicated to my <b>dear friend (haha) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/18104163' rel='nofollow noopener'>Navessa</a></b> who was thoughtful enough to challenge me to read this book. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Did you people seriously think I would willingly chose to read something like this? Are you insane? <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></i><br/><br/><b>My name is Sarah and I'm a survivor</b>. <br/><br/><b>Yes I am. Because I have done it</b>. I have read all 384 pages of this Historical Romance masterpiece. And I am still alive to talk about it. <b>Someone please give me a medal</b>.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429976707i/14654705._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Where to begin?</b> The possibilities are quite </span>
  <span id="freeText13715563213382984385" style="display:none"><i>This review is dedicated to my <b>dear friend (haha) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/18104163" rel="nofollow noopener">Navessa</a></b> who was thoughtful enough to challenge me to read this book. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Did you people seriously think I would willingly chose to read something like this? Are you insane? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></i><br><br><b>My name is Sarah and I'm a survivor</b>. <br><br><b>Yes I am. Because I have done it</b>. I have read all 384 pages of this Historical Romance masterpiece. And I am still alive to talk about it. <b>Someone please give me a medal</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429976707i/14654705._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Where to begin?</b> The possibilities are quite endless. Let's start with the obvious shall we?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430003677i/14663675.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Need I say more? Didn't think so. Moving on.<br><br>►► <b>The sheer stupidity of this book is staggering</b>. I didn't expect to either like or enjoy it but this went beyond my wildest imaginings. Stupid, non-existent, boring plot! Stupid, clichéd characters! Stupid, manufactured, artificial, ridiculous drama! <b>Stupid everything! Yay</b>! <br><br>►► <b>Meet Daphne, our heroine</b>: she's a pathetic idiot with <b>TSTL tendencies</b> who manipulates the shit out of people and doesn't seem to understand <b>the meaning of the word NO</b>. But hey, she's got a great excuse: she's <b>naïve and inexperienced</b>! She doesn't realize she's doing anything wrong! <b>WTF?!</b> <i>[phone rings in the background]</i> <b>Me</b>: hello? <b>Julia Quinn</b>: I'm sorry to interrupt this delightfully enlightening review but I can't let you insult poor Daphne here. <b>Me</b>: you have got to be kidding me. <b>Julia Quinn</b>: no no, I assure you I'm quite serious. Dear old Daff might be a teensy bit naïve but she's witty and clever! <b>Me</b>: err, excuse me but there's a difference between being naïve and being <b>a total, complete twit</b>. Bye now.<br><br>►► <b>Meet Simon, our hero</b>: he's one of the flattest, <b>most ridiculous, idiotic characters</b> I've ever come across. <i>[phone rings in the background]</i> <b>Me</b>: bloody hell, I'll never manage to write this stupid review for this stupid book. <b>Julia Quinn</b>: I'm sorry to interrupt this delightfully enlightening review again but I can't let you insult poor Simon here. <b>Me</b>: watch it woman, I can be quite the homicidal maniac when I want to. <b>Julia Quinn</b>: oh dear. Such violence! I mean no harm, I promise. I only wish to make you understand how wonderfully dashing, rakish and yet very complex Simon is. <b>Me</b>: excuse me but there's a difference between being complex and being a <b>pathetically clichéd rake wannabe</b>. Bye now.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430003677i/14663676.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Oh will you people just chill for a second?! This gif applies to this section up here ↑↑↑, not this one right there ↓↓↓. You know I ♥ you all (sometimes) despite your appalling taste in books.</i><br><br>►► <b>Most of my friends</b> who read this delightful piece of literature keep mentioning its overflowing humour and witty banter. Right. <b>Let's explore our options here</b>:<br><br>➘ <b>Option A</b>: I have no sense of humour at all and my wit radar is temporarily out of order.<br>➘ <b>Option B</b>: above mentioned friends have clearly lost it.<br>➘ <b>Option C</b>: above mentioned friends were actually talking about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9431334-the-duke-and-i?from_search=true&amp;search_exp_group=group_a&amp;search_version=service" rel="nofollow noopener">this book</a>. <br><br><i>Option A can be discarded right away because I obviously have a fantastic sense of humour and my wit radar is performing quite spectacularly these days. I'd go for option B but if I say so my friend list may plummet. Option C it is.</i><br><br>►► <b>The Sleeping Pill Club</b>: Julia Quinn, you can be proud of yourself. You have officially joined the likes of V.E. Schwab, Diana Gabaldon, Charlaine Harris, Stacia Kane and J.C Daniels in this very exclusive club. Congratulations! You have completely mastered total and utter boredom! <b>The cure for insomnia is held in your <s> witty banter</s> blah blah blah blah!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430003677i/14663677.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>►► <b>The sexy</b>: you know that feeling you get when you're reading great smut and you're suddenly in dire need of a cold shower? <b>Think of this book as the cold shower</b>. Believe me, you won't be throwing your underwear across the room while reading this story. The make out/sex scenes are even more lacklustre here than they are in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/301082.Dead_Until_Dark?from_search=true&amp;search_exp_group=group_a&amp;search_version=service" rel="nofollow noopener">Dead Until Dark</a>. I kid you not. Julia Quinn, I commend you for this latest achievement. <b>There is no way in hell I could get pregnant from this</b>. <br><br>►► <b>Brow gymnastics</b>: What, pray tell, is this mysterious disease? I do hope it isn't contagious. I have to say there is so much brow action going on in this book I was quite exhausted by the time I turned the last page. <b>There are more than 50 instances of brow gymnastics here</b>. The poor characters' brows are in turn: doubtful, raising, rising, drown together, scrunched, arched, wrinkled, lifted, knit together, quirked and wiggled. <b>Spocky has nothing on these people</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430003678i/14663678.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>►► <b>I am in a very lenient mood today</b> so I shall forgive the author for putting me through all this and will actually go as far as offering her <b>some friendly advice</b>:<br><br>① <b>To make your plot more exciting</b>: call 1-800-IA, the Ilona Andrews emergency hotline. This week only: 30% discount on <b>Character Development 101</b> classes.<br><br>② <b>To help with the humour and witty banter</b>: call 1-800-Oscar, the Oscar Wilde emergency hotline. In case you can't get through (Oscar operators are in high demand), consider reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/92303.The_Importance_of_Being_Earnest?from_search=true&amp;search_exp_group=group_b&amp;search_version=service" rel="nofollow noopener">The Importance of Being Earnest</a> to get an idea of <b>what wit really is</b>.<br> <br>③ <b>For sex scenes that get your readers "boom! Pregnant!"</b>: please call 1-800-JZB, the Jericho Barrons emergency hotline. Your case being particularly desperate, please press #4 after the recorded message. You will be redirected to the dedicated Book 4 Chapter 4 line. Listen carefully and <b>you might learn a thing or two</b>. <br><br><i>Don't be shy, Julia Quinn! Call the emergency hotlines now, you'll be glad you did! And remember, there are no stupid questions, so ask away! </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430005421ra/14664010.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>💌 <b>To all my <s>dear</s> friends who loved this book</b>: shush now, it's okay, I promise you will be fine. We will find a nice big house for you where lovely people dressed in crisp white uniforms will take good care of you. They will give you cute little blue pills every morning and they will dress you in a lovely white jacket with very fashionable (if a bit unusual) sleeves. <b>You will love it</b>.<br><br>💌 <b>To <s>thoughtful</s> Navessa</b>: just wipe that smug look off your face and pass the vodka will you? <br><br>►► <b>One last piece of advice</b> to all you well-meaning human beings out there: the next person who sends me a Historical Romance rec is dead meat. <b>Just sayin'.</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_3060326146" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3060326146" />
    <a title="Merphy Napier" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41973734-merphy-napier"><img alt="Merphy Napier" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524921716p2/41973734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3060326146?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merphy Napier" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merphy Napier" href="/user/show/41973734-merphy-napier">Merphy Napier</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41973734-merphy-napier?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41973734-merphy-napier?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41973734-merphy-napier?shelf=one-star">one-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3060326146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9750751070429656336">Okay here we go. I read this because it's my friend's favorite and she wanted me to give it a go. I think it's important to try new things because I've fallen in love with genres this way. Unfortunately, I really didn't like this, and here's why:<br/><br/>What I liked:<br/>- The build up for this romance was really well done. The characters had great chemistry when they were falling in love.<br/>- My initial intro to the characters was great, easy to latch on to them<br/>- The male MC has a stutter. My son has a stutter</span>
  <span id="freeText9750751070429656336" style="display:none">Okay here we go. I read this because it's my friend's favorite and she wanted me to give it a go. I think it's important to try new things because I've fallen in love with genres this way. Unfortunately, I really didn't like this, and here's why:<br /><br />What I liked:<br />- The build up for this romance was really well done. The characters had great chemistry when they were falling in love.<br />- My initial intro to the characters was great, easy to latch on to them<br />- The male MC has a stutter. My son has a stutter and seeing the Duke's struggle hit me in my mommy heart.<br /><br />What I didn't like (oh boy here we go)<br />- Our female MC was really smart... until she wasn't. Then she was really *really* not. Daf has four brothers. We're reminded of this a lot. She's really wise, sassy, and knows that the Duke is a "Rake" (player) with lots of experience, which doesn't intimidate her. Until the night before her wedding. Suddenly, the girl knows less than a houseplant. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ This intelligent, intuitive woman who pays attention to her brothers and the people around her, who is in her 20's, has no idea how babies are made. And is shocked when she learns you have to have sex. Then, she's shocked to learn sex can be just for fun. This is not a product of her time. I've read a lot of classics and while it was a very different time, women were not left this in the dark. The way the whole scene plays out is way over the top  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />- The Duke SUCKS <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ he tells her he can't have kids. She accepts this and they get married anyway. He then will have sex with her and pull out. And Daf just things, "I wonder why he does that, oh well" Until she finally realizes what he's doing and that he's *choosing* not to get her pregnant, then they have a big blow up. It's totally fine if you don't want kids, but you don't take advantage of your wife's ignorance. Not in day to day life, and not in the bedroom.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />- Daf SUCKS even MORE <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ So yeah, she's mad at him for lying, manipulating, and taking advantage of her ignorance. So she rapes him. After their big fight, he goes and gets drunk, then comes home and begs her to take him back. They fall asleep next to each other, then she wakes him up in the night, get's on top of him (this is important) and starts having sex with him. He's happy to do this, until he realizes he needs to pull out, but she's in a position of leverage (being on top) and he's still drunk so not as in control. HE PHYSICALLY SAYS TO HER "Stop, please, I don't want -" and she holds him down so he has no choice but to ejaculate inside her. He did not consent to this kind of sex. At this point, she knows why he doesn't want to get pregnant, knows why he has been having sex the way he has up to this point (still messed up it took this lsong, sex is not something you don't communicate about), and she still forces him to have sex in a way that he says "no" and "stop" to. This is rape.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />- There are no consequences. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ They then have another fight but Simon's stutter comes back so he leaves. He's gone for a few days. Daf thinks to herself "Did I take advantage of him? Probably. But I don't feel bad about it. I fell great, that could have been my only chance to get pregnant." Then, she sends a letter off to Simon to let him know she's pregnant. He comes to terms with it and comes home. By the time he gets home, she's learned that she wasn't pregnant, just late for her period. She's upset. They talk about it and he decides that maybe he's okay with a baby. She says she thought he was mad because of what she did. He says he didn't like that she raped him, but that's not why he was mad (the word rape is never actually used in this book, but I'm calling it what it is). He was actually just made because he was stuttering and he was embarrassed. Then they make up, Simon works through his problems, and they decide they want a baby together, and live happily ever after. Yay! No one's mad about the rape, or lack of consent in either partner throughout the entire relationship. What a wonderful love story!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />So basically, this was a really abusive and disturbing relationship where both parties didn't treat the other one with any respect at all and were selfish the entire time. But it's painted as a really cute romance. Sure, the characters are meant to be seen as flawed, but it still looks romantic. I would disagree. I don't see this as a romance at all.<br /><br />I know this is a well loved book so just to be clear, I'm not telling anyone what to love or hate - just writing how I felt while reading this book. &lt;3</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_112219455" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112219455" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2043222-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577660807p2/2043222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112219455?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/2043222-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112219455" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer876962550290196851"><a href='http://gotfiction.com/review-the-duke-and-i-by-julia-quinn/' rel='nofollow noopener'>review posted on Got Fiction? Books</a><br/><br/>2.5<br/>A lot of my GR buddies love this book, and a few have recommended it to me. So I ordered it, and up until a certain part in the end, I really was enjoying it.<br/><br/><b>I won't feel bad about the spoilers in here, because this is an older book, and a ton of people have read it.</b><br/><br/>I liked Daphne, and I really liked Daphne and Simon's interactions, witty reparte, banter. all of the above. Obviously they were meant for each other, and not in the sickeningly sweet sort of way</span>
  <span id="freeText876962550290196851" style="display:none"><a href="http://gotfiction.com/review-the-duke-and-i-by-julia-quinn/" rel="nofollow noopener">review posted on Got Fiction? Books</a><br /><br />2.5<br />A lot of my GR buddies love this book, and a few have recommended it to me. So I ordered it, and up until a certain part in the end, I really was enjoying it.<br /><br /><b>I won't feel bad about the spoilers in here, because this is an older book, and a ton of people have read it.</b><br /><br />I liked Daphne, and I really liked Daphne and Simon's interactions, witty reparte, banter. all of the above. Obviously they were meant for each other, and not in the sickeningly sweet sort of way. They were fun to watch together. <br /><br />I hated Simon's father. Hated him so much. What a bastard. Simon at one point said his father wanted an heir, not a son. So well put. <br />The two of them decided to fake an interest in each other so that all the match-making mamas would leave Simon alone, and Daphne could have better prospects, because with a handsome duke interested in her, suddenly every man finds her lovely. At one point, Daphne has 6 suitors (7 if you count Simon) in one room, and one is reciting poetry (bad poetry) from one knee for her! Too funny, their plan was actually working!<br /><br />But around 200 pages in or so, it all began to lose some of its appeal. Daphne is bossy...no problem there, I'm bossy, totally works for me. But she becomes more arrogant than bossy at one point, and this is right around the part where Daphne's brother catches Simon with his mouth on Daphne's breast. He says "Marry my sister or else!" or something as cliched. Simon, who we all have known since moment one, is never going to marry. Simon tells Daphne that, Anthony and Benedick (her brothers) tell Daphne that. But still Daphne feels (even though Simon never claimed any feelings of any sort towards her) that Simon cares enough for her to marry her instead of duel with Anthony. Wrong, Simon would never raise a pistol at his friend Anthony, so he goes in with the assumption that he will die. <br /><br />Daphne says <i>"I-I've always known that I wasn't the sort of woman men dreamed of, but I never thought anyone would prefer death to marriage with me."</i><br /><br />Wow, that line made me want Simon to explain things to her. He says <i>"If it could be anyone it would be you."</i> which was heartbreaking, but not enough. <br /><br />So, Daphne gets her other brother Colin to take her to the duel so she can scam the duke into marriage-she tells him people saw them in a compromising position and he just has to marry her so she won't be labeled damaged goods. I didn't buy it. yes some folks saw them leave together but it was still manipulating. That is where I began to dislike Daphne. She manipulated him into marriage trying to justify that he might not want to live, but he might live to save her. It made no sense to me. She pressured him for marriage, got it, and they were actually happy for a while, but to me it felt hollow.<br /><br />Daphne found out from the housekeeper what kind of childhood Simon really had, and about his awful father who berated him, then declared him dead to any who would listen, all because Simon stuttered as a boy. <br /><br /><b>***SPOILERS***</b><br />Daphne finally understood that when Simon said he couldn't have children, he didn't mean he couldn't father them, but rather that he could never be a father...he <i>wouldn't</i> have children. Her dream of a family was dead.<br /><br />What bugs me here are 2 things:<br /><b>1.</b> She went in knowing no children would result<br /><b>2.</b> When Simon was drunk and aroused and she wouldn't let him pull out. <br /><br />That sobered him up pretty quickly. That whole scene was a mess-she was wrong. Absolutely manipulative and wrong. Simon was absolutely right to be furious. That drunken scene was sweet and touching and funny and then...that. I was so angry because Daphne then rationalized to herself that it's not like she went in thinking "I'm going to force him to come inside me." She did. She said she felt powerful and loved it.<br /><br />And for her to not explain to her family that he was angry because she did something, to let them think Simon was a prick for his boorish behavior, really made me lose a lot of respect for both Daphne and Julia Quinn.<br /><br />Simon was the one who had to apologize-yes he lied, I was mad he never clarified, but good Lord...Daphne just infuriated me.<br /><br />So, the book was good til Daphne became a master manipulator. For her to give Simon ultimatums about no sex until you say we can have children was selfish and pretty messed up of her.<br /><br />The ending was sweet, but not sweet enough for me to forgive the mess Daphne made of Simon's/<i>their</i> life/future.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="876962550290196851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1198670078" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1198670078" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1198670078?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=regency">regency</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1198670078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12128177742251004745"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Can there be any greater challenge to London’s Ambitious Mamas than an unmarried duke?” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Well <i>my</i> Mama refused to find me a duke, even though she is desperate to see me settled down (apparently, I am a spinster at the ripe age of 24). In fact, she laughed at the idea, and then started her "stop reading-start living" lectures, while arranging to introduce me to the Lady of the Caramel's son, who is "rich, young and available"(I think available is her most important quality). Me, well, </span>
  <span id="freeText12128177742251004745" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Can there be any greater challenge to London’s Ambitious Mamas than an unmarried duke?” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Well <i>my</i> Mama refused to find me a duke, even though she is desperate to see me settled down (apparently, I am a spinster at the ripe age of 24). In fact, she laughed at the idea, and then started her "stop reading-start living" lectures, while arranging to introduce me to the Lady of the Caramel's son, who is "rich, young and available"(I think available is her most important quality). Me, well, I ignored her as per usual, and started spinning, following the notes of an imaginary melody, pretending I was dancing with a handsome, sexy and mysterious duke (or prince, I'm not picky).<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476641506ra/20865775.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Because that's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/110391.The_Duke_and_I__Bridgertons___1_" title="The Duke and I (Bridgertons, #1) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">The Duke and I</a>'s major effect; <b>daydreaming</b>.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There were rules among friends, commandments, really, and the most important one was Thou Shalt Not Lust After Thy Friend's Sister.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>But Simon Basset couldn't help it. Daphne Bridgerton haunted his dreams, evoking dark fantasies that could not see daylight. There was something about her, something that made him forget who he was and what he was, she was the perfect match for him. She challenged him. But he had taken an oath, and he was determined to keep it. No matter how much he wanted her.<br><br>Daphne Bridgerton was not a popular debutante. She was witty (perhaps too witty for her own good) , and gentle, but not the kind of woman that would inspire poems and make men go crazy over her. But Simon Basset was different. He made her heart race and her body burn, and when he proposed an arrangement that would benefit them both, Daphne could not refuse. But she also couldn't stop hoping that one day this wonderful man would become hers, body and soul. That she would tear down the walls he was building for years.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“When you smile it takes up half your face.'<br>'Simon!' she exclaimed. 'That sounds horrible.'<br>'It's enchanting.'<br>'Distorted.'<br>'Desirable.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I've been dreaming of balls and gowns since I was a little girl. I still close my eyes and place myself in fairytales, and a part of me whispers that I was born in the wrong century. <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/63898.Julia_Quinn" title="Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Julia Quinn</a> satisfied every girly fantasy I've ever had, and then some more.</b> She had a <b>Jane Austen vibe</b>, but added <b>sizzling tension, steam to make you drool, and a not so gentle gentleman</b> (imagine a dirtier Mr. Darcy, with many issues but always eager to please a woman). It was <b>delicious</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476642770ra/20865923.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/110391.The_Duke_and_I__Bridgertons___1_" title="The Duke and I (Bridgertons, #1) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">The Duke and I</a> was a <b>light, entertaining and uttetly addicting novel</b>. Every time I turned its pages, a brand new old world opened before my eyes, sucking me into a society that demanded of women good manners and healthy heirs but gave them nothing in return, a London shocked but mesmerized by Lady Whistledown’s gossip papers, ballrooms full of Ambitious Mamas that became the nightmare of every eligible bachelor, and a loud family whose banters cracked me up. I must admit there were times I wanted to punch Simon for being so stubborn, guided by the hatred towards his father, but I also ached for his difficult childhood and the lack of love and acceptance that marked him. But Daphne knew that she could cure him and fight his demons, I admired her for her persistance and devotion, and I could empathize with her. Simon and Daphne were an explosive couple, that <b>warmed my heart <i>and</i> my cheeks</b>!<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The world seemed somehow different when one was lying down. Darker, more dangerous ... And in that moment, as he slowly closed the distance between them, he became her entire world.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>In this world, I was a debutante. An innocent girl seduced by a devilishly handsome duke. A woman determined to fight for the man she loved.<br>And I savoured every single moment.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454049674ra/17908483.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="12128177742251004745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=sucked">sucked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=england">england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=fluffy">fluffy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=rape-abuse">rape-abuse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer93238552&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer93238552" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10648167840405412151">I never thought that I could have a whole book spoiled for me by one action, but this book proved that I could. What's so irritating about this is that I was enjoying the book. I liked the character's amusing dialogue and the friendship the developed.<br/><br/>Things did start to go a bit downhill for me when Daphne chases Simon down at the duel. I don't get the most optimistic feeling when I see someone willing to die rather than marry. I know it wasn't Daphne in particular, but when the hero has so much</span>
  <span id="freeText10648167840405412151" style="display:none">I never thought that I could have a whole book spoiled for me by one action, but this book proved that I could. What's so irritating about this is that I was enjoying the book. I liked the character's amusing dialogue and the friendship the developed.<br /><br />Things did start to go a bit downhill for me when Daphne chases Simon down at the duel. I don't get the most optimistic feeling when I see someone willing to die rather than marry. I know it wasn't Daphne in particular, but when the hero has so much baggage that death is preferable to his other options I know the road ahead is not going to be smooth. I started to get nervous about how something with that weight would be handled by the author. She has skill but in all the books I've read by her they all seemed very light and not really serious at all. I was willing to go along for the ride though.<br /><br />In some ways I wish I had stopped reading half way through and never got such a bad taste in my mouth. I know that Simon lied by omission in letting Daphne assume he wouldn't have kids because he couldn't have them. But who can really blame him? He was ashamed of how he was when he was a kid. If he would have said he just plain wouldn't have kids she would have demanded to know why and he would have had to explain all his humiliation. Who would willingly do that? She had to maneuver him into marrying her in the first place. He would have rather died in the duel than marry her and be put in that situation! She was even the one that initiated the situation that led to them having to marry! She seems to forget it was all her idea toward the end.<br /><br />I just can't help but think that the whole conflict in this book was manufactured by Daphne. The way the book was written seems to make Simon seem like the bad guy when what she did to him was unforgivable. I was ready for Simon to find someone new after that. I can't believe he came back and actually apologized to her. She tried to take a baby from him by force! I'm sorry I know he was into it, but he was drunk and didn't realized she wouldn't let him pull away at the end. When he realized he started struggling. That right there is force. If a man had done that to a girl there would have been a lot more people upset by it.<br /><br />I know that Daphne made a token statement about being okay with him not wanting kids if it was for the right reason, but I doubt that. She was consumed by the thought of children like she wouldn't have been complete without them. Besides, she may not have agreed with his reasons, but who is she to try and say he doesn't have a right to feel that way?<br /><br />I don't know if I'll read anymore of her. I've read her other Bridgerton books (and decided to finally read the 1st one) and I thought most of them were ok, but this one really disturbed me. I don't know if I want to risk feeling like that again. I read to watch two people fall in love, not to watch someone try to force her husband to impregnate her.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10648167840405412151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3597320784" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3597320784" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3597320784?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780749907730" href="/book/show/298367.The_Duke_and_I">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3597320784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1003879463736411829">I am not sure what to rate this book so for now I’m leaving it blank. <br/><br/>I mainly read this because Shonda freakin’ Rhimes is creating the Netflix series. And also because I adore historical romances and Julia Quinn is well loved. <br/><br/>Up until the scene, this book was pretty much perfect. The introduction to the Bridgerton family was amazing. The relationship that began to develop between Daphne and Simon was equally as amazing. Their buildup and their overall chemistry was one of the best things I’ve </span>
  <span id="freeText1003879463736411829" style="display:none">I am not sure what to rate this book so for now I’m leaving it blank. <br /><br />I mainly read this because Shonda freakin’ Rhimes is creating the Netflix series. And also because I adore historical romances and Julia Quinn is well loved. <br /><br />Up until the scene, this book was pretty much perfect. The introduction to the Bridgerton family was amazing. The relationship that began to develop between Daphne and Simon was equally as amazing. Their buildup and their overall chemistry was one of the best things I’ve come across in historical romance. Or romance in general because it flowed so fuckin’ beautifully. <br /><br />However, we get to that unfortunate scene and I was beyond uncomfortable reading it. I found myself skim reading the book somewhat afterwards because it left a bad taste in my mouth. My enjoyment started waning. <br />I don’t classify it as rape but consent was definitely a major issue for me and the feelings Simon expressed were completely disregarded even though the act itself at the time was consensual. But it read as abuse. It bordered onto rape. <br /><br />Like many said, if the roles were reversed, it would have been screamed about. But the roles don’t need to be reversed in order for the gravity of the situation to be understood. The time this book was published does play a part into the consent issue and has to be taken into account. That nuance and dialogue we have now of discussing what consent is and is not did not exist then as far as my knowledge goes. Hence why this was overlooked by the publishing industry. <br /> <br />Thank god we’ve come a long way since then. <br /><br />So if you do decide to read this, at least be aware you are coming across a scene that is problematic and the experience will differ for every reader. <br /><br />I’m not writing this book or author off. I just wish it was dealt with in a different way. But we live and we learn.</span>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=kissing-books">kissing-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=regency">regency</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2123427300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7887353424282610156"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>I think it's been a while since I've seen such an even split among my friends when it comes to how they rated the book. Half my friends <i>loved </i>THE DUKE AND I and the other half apparently hated it. The <i>Bridgertons </i>series is Julia Quinn's most famous historical romance offering so I've been wanting to read it for a while, but I'm not unfamiliar with her work. In my opinion, she's a bit notorious for over-aggressive heroines who come across</span>
  <span id="freeText7887353424282610156" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>I think it's been a while since I've seen such an even split among my friends when it comes to how they rated the book. Half my friends <i>loved </i>THE DUKE AND I and the other half apparently hated it. The <i>Bridgertons </i>series is Julia Quinn's most famous historical romance offering so I've been wanting to read it for a while, but I'm not unfamiliar with her work. In my opinion, she's a bit notorious for over-aggressive heroines who come across as petulant and bitchy and Big Misunderstandings that are especially stupid and tends to draw them out for extra dramatic tension in the last act.<br><br><br><br>The titular duke, Simon Basset, is cast in your typical damaged hero mold of "I slut around because I have daddy issues." In his case, the issues are probably warranted. He didn't speak until he was four years old, and when he did, it was with a stutter. After his dad basically rage-quits on parenting, Simon is left on his own, unloved, except for the tender hand of his nurse. His father basically disowns him, telling his servants and all his friends that he has no son, and refuses to answer any of his correspondence.<br><br><br><br>Of course, once Simon is able to overcome all of this and become the most desired bachelor in the ton, his father is secretly pleased and ready to take pride in his son because hurray, Simon got over his stutter and that means that he isn't mentally defunct, i.e. "an idiot." Simon is so over his dad, though, and since breeding, honor, and titles are all that matter to his father, he has vowed never to have children so that the Hastings line dies with him, and all the property will cede to his cousins.<br><br><br><br>Daphne, the heroine, is part of the Bridgerton family, and the daughter of a viscount. They name their children like hurricanes, in alphabetical order, chronologically, so Daphne is the fourth-born child (as well as the oldest daughter). She's also a bit of a wallflower and a spinster-in-the-making, and her mother is determined to make a match. Daphne's brothers are friends with Simon, and they end up meeting at a party when Simon saves her from a creepy friend-zoned suitor who won't take no for an answer. They end up liking each other, although Simon denies his attraction once he's figured out that she's the off-limits sister of his friend. They decide to pretend to have developed a <i>tendre </i>for one another, to keep Simon's unwanted suitors at bay while also making Daphne <i>more </i>desirable. Too bad that he ends up compromising her and Daphne's oldest brother, Anthony, calls him out at dawn.<br><br><br><br>Knowing that Simon's honor will lead him to not fire, and that Anthony's rage on her behalf will undoubtedly result in a killing shot, Daphne demands that they be married and Simon protests, much to Daphne's hurt (because he'd rather be dead than marry her? ouch). He tells her that he can't have children and that since she's always yapping about wanting a <i>Little Women </i>type family, he doesn't want her to be unhappy. Daphne tells him he's worth it and insists. And it seems like this actually might be a cute little love story...until Daphne rapes her husband in order to forcibly get him to impregnate her. That's right, when Simon is drunk, Daphne mounts him and then hunkers down on him so that he has no choice but to come inside her, and she is so smug and so pleased, thinking that she has "fixed" him and then has the <i>gall </i>to cry and get all teary and sanctimonious when he is angry.<br><br><br><br>My friends had warned me about this scene going in, but reading it still left a hugely bitter taste in my mouth. Now, I do want to say that as a reader of bodice-rippers, I am no stranger to unconsensual scenes in books. But there is a major difference between acts of rape in which the rapist is depicted as a rapist, and acts of rape in which the rapist is depicted as having the moral high ground. This is part of the reason sexism is so harmful: not just because women are victimized or robbed of agency, but also because people don't ever think that women can be the perpetrators of physical or sexual violence, because they are so "harmless," and so we get bullshit scenes like this.<br><br><br><br>Daphne can fuck right off.<br><br><br><br>1.5 to 2 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="7887353424282610156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/348571878?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" href="/user/show/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship">Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780749936570" href="/book/show/1859059.The_Duke_and_I">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=1st-in-series">1st-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=laugh-out-loud">laugh-out-loud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=british">british</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=series-abandoned">series-abandoned</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=rape">rape</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer348571878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4711195501936807438"><b>It's okay to rape your husband</b>. (Source: Chapter 18 onwards.)<br/><br/>Up until this chapter <i>The Duke and I</i> was on the road to four stars. Four and not five because of:<br/><br/>➜ Anthony's behaviour after witnessing his friend's mouth on his sister's chest in the garden of a house party, challenging his <b>FRIEND</b> to a duel after Simon refused to marry Daphne on the grounds it would make her unhappy because he couldn't give her what she'd always wanted i.e. children and therefore happiness. If Simon really was a frien</span>
  <span id="freeText4711195501936807438" style="display:none"><b>It's okay to rape your husband</b>. (Source: Chapter 18 onwards.)<br /><br />Up until this chapter <i>The Duke and I</i> was on the road to four stars. Four and not five because of:<br /><br />➜ Anthony's behaviour after witnessing his friend's mouth on his sister's chest in the garden of a house party, challenging his <b>FRIEND</b> to a duel after Simon refused to marry Daphne on the grounds it would make her unhappy because he couldn't give her what she'd always wanted i.e. children and therefore happiness. If Simon really was a friend, Anthony would've asked more questions about the why and been more tenacious in getting an accurate answer instead of jumping into a duel where he'd be forced to kill his friend;<br /><br />➜ The following duel scene the next morning when Daphne outright lies to Simon about others, besides Anthony, witnessing their intimate act to prevent Simon from being killed in the duel and to force him to marry her, followed by Simon omitting the fact he won't have children and instead says he 'can't' have them so he doesn't have to tell her his very personal reason why.<br /><br />I swallowed these things hoping it would come out later and they'd forgive each other in the end.<br /><br />What I was not expecting was Daphne's grotesque arrogance and selfishness in taking advantage of her drunk husband after she found out the truth, denying him sex and companionship, and not allowing him to pull out during sex so she could have the children she'd always wanted. They'd been <b>MARRIED TWO WEEKS</b>, there was plenty of time to discuss his problems, his worries, about even contemplating children and instead she takes the choice from him against his will as he struggles with her once he realises her intentions. <br /><br />After what Simon's father did to him Daphne's behaviour is even worse because she knew about Simon's stuttering and his father's abandonment of Simon because of this. And then two months after Simon leaves her he finds he misses her and he <b>CAN'T REMEMBER WHY HE LEFT IN THE FIRST PLACE</b>, thereby excusing any wrongdoing on her part. But not only that, Daphne sends her angry brother after Simon without telling him she was the reason Simon left and not Simon himself. <br /><br />So, four stars to one. If the gender roles had been reversed I'd expect more people would've been outraged at the rape. Completely ruined a perfectly good book, and my first, and possibly the last, by Julia Quinn.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4711195501936807438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17334872463971734778"><b>4.5 Simon makes my heart stutter Stars</b><br/><br/><a href='https://imgur.com/2XbSPPa' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1544474894ra/26724144.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>The Duke and I has been on my TBR list for years, but I just never got around to reading it. Now I can't believe I waited so long. I wasn't two chapters into this book before I knew two things for sure 1. I loved the Bridgertons and 2. Julia Quinn would be a new favorite author. This book grabbed me right out the gate. It captivated my heart, and I fell in love with this big, loud but sweet family. This book was cute, at times sad and had me laughing out</span>
  <span id="freeText17334872463971734778" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Simon makes my heart stutter Stars</b><br><br><a href="https://imgur.com/2XbSPPa" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1544474894ra/26724144.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The Duke and I has been on my TBR list for years, but I just never got around to reading it. Now I can't believe I waited so long. I wasn't two chapters into this book before I knew two things for sure 1. I loved the Bridgertons and 2. Julia Quinn would be a new favorite author. This book grabbed me right out the gate. It captivated my heart, and I fell in love with this big, loud but sweet family. This book was cute, at times sad and had me laughing out loud more times than I can count. <br><br><a href="https://imgur.com/VNETUjG" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1544474894ra/26724143.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Simon totally broke my heart. It bled for the way his dad was to him, and for all he had to suffer because of it. Simon was damaged but he was still a great guy. Daphne was funny, sassy, and very independent. I loved that she was honest and didn't play games when it came to how she felt. <br><br><a href="https://imgur.com/a96dS9i" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1544474894ra/26724142.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Simon and Daphne were very sweet together. They had a strong connection from their first meeting. I loved them as a couple. They weren't perfect they messed up, did things that hurt the other, but in real life love is messy and people are imperfect. Simon and Daphne's missteps made them more human, and relatable. I loved Daphne's whole family. Her older 3 brothers really had a cute protective roll in this book. I can't wait to read their books too. I also loved her mom. The whole family was very cute and endearing. Overall a great read and I think Julia Quinn has herself a new fan girl. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1540865561" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4440376666103275436"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472750173i/20237706._SX540_.jpg' width='200' height='150' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Disappointed. Actually, disappointed doesn't even begin to describe it.</b><br/><br/><i>*Unpopular opinion time*</i><br/><br/>Once upon a time, I wasn't into historical romance. I thought they were silly and anti-women, and I wasn't even interested in <i>trying</i> them. Thankfully, I discovered historical romances by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2752928.Tessa_Dare' title='Tessa Dare' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tessa Dare</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2906892.Courtney_Milan' title='Courtney Milan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Courtney Milan</a>, and I fell head over heels for the genre. <br/><br/><b>I'm thanking my lucky stars that I didn't try this book first because I fear I would have never read the genre again. </b><br/><br/>I've been meaning to try th</span>
  <span id="freeText4440376666103275436" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472750173i/20237706._SX540_.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Disappointed. Actually, disappointed doesn't even begin to describe it.</b><br><br><i>*Unpopular opinion time*</i><br><br>Once upon a time, I wasn't into historical romance. I thought they were silly and anti-women, and I wasn't even interested in <i>trying</i> them. Thankfully, I discovered historical romances by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2752928.Tessa_Dare" title="Tessa Dare" rel="nofollow noopener">Tessa Dare</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2906892.Courtney_Milan" title="Courtney Milan" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Milan</a>, and I fell head over heels for the genre. <br><br><b>I'm thanking my lucky stars that I didn't try this book first because I fear I would have never read the genre again. </b><br><br>I've been meaning to try this series for some time now. I've read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/63898.Julia_Quinn" title="Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Julia Quinn</a> before, and I really liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25657772.Because_of_Miss_Bridgerton__Rokesbys___1_" title="Because of Miss Bridgerton (Rokesbys, #1) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Because of Miss Bridgerton</a>. EVERYONE has told me to try the original Bridgerton series, starting with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/110391.The_Duke_and_I__Bridgertons___1_" title="The Duke and I (Bridgertons, #1) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">The Duke and I</a>. So, of course, I decided to take the series on, and I even bought the next couple of books following the first. However, I'm absolutely flummoxed by the love for this book. <br><br>Daphne Bridgerton was the <b>worst heroine that I've read in a long time</b>. She is meant to be strong and spunky, but I thought that she was <b>self-serving and TSTL</b>. I actually hated her. She manipulated poor Simon every step of the way. She forced him to befriend her, she forced him to marry her, and forced him in other ways that found absolutely <b>morally reprehensible</b>. She was vile, truly, and thought herself to be entirely blameless throughout the story. <br><br>Simon didn't quite make sense either. He had a rakish reputations, one that I didn't see any evidence of in the story, and had a twisted mentality about his situation. He was <b>self-pitying and broody</b>, and though I didn't like him, I thought he got the short end of the stick being stuck with Daphne. <br><br>To top it off, <b>the book was way too long</b>, and it took me ages to finish the audiobook. I wasn't motivated to keep listening, even with a <b>flawless narration</b> from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/474459.Rosalyn_Landor" title="Rosalyn Landor" rel="nofollow noopener">Rosalyn Landor</a>, who did her very best to add personality and sympathy for these odious characters. <br><br>I know, a very <b>unpopular opinion</b>, but this book only gets as high as 2-stars because of the narration. Otherwise, it would be in 1-star territory.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time" rel="nofollow noopener">goodreads</a>|<a href="https://www.instagram.com/reading_all_night_long/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a>|<a href="https://twitter.com/DentistHeatherK" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a>|<a href="http://www.myfictionnook.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a></span>

<div id="review_36758161" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36758161" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36758161?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of light Regencies with a bit of angst</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=hero-i-liked">hero-i-liked</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36758161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13919136445461053127">When I read a book, I want to become involved emotionally. A book that does that is more likely to be highly rated. Such was the case with The Duke and I.<br/><br/>I have a sickness, an infatuation for tortured, dark, conflicted heroes. The happy-go-lucky guys don't capture my imagination nearly so much as their darker counterparts. Fortunately, Simon was tortured enough to keep me happy.<br/><br/>The beginning of this book was brilliantly done. I was already captivated with Simon, the future Duke of Hastings. My h</span>
  <span id="freeText13919136445461053127" style="display:none">When I read a book, I want to become involved emotionally. A book that does that is more likely to be highly rated. Such was the case with The Duke and I.<br /><br />I have a sickness, an infatuation for tortured, dark, conflicted heroes. The happy-go-lucky guys don't capture my imagination nearly so much as their darker counterparts. Fortunately, Simon was tortured enough to keep me happy.<br /><br />The beginning of this book was brilliantly done. I was already captivated with Simon, the future Duke of Hastings. My heart cried for him. I wanted to see him overcome the obstacles that were unfairly set before him, to become the man he was capable of being. And boy, did he become quite a man.<br /><br />Imagine my surprise, that for all my affinity for Simon, that the star of this story was Daphne? She started out very mild, sweet (typical Regency heroine), not necessarily standing out. But, by the end of this book, I loved her. She was just the woman that Simon needed. He was what she wanted, and she was going to get her man, and wouldn't settle for less than all of him. She had mettle, and she wasn't afraid to challenge Simon to change the future, and to shake free from the chains of the past, which held him prisoner. Perhaps he never would have found true happiness and joy if Daphne had not hammered (gently and not so gently, at times) at the walls around his heart.<br /><br />The event that puts a strain on their marriage could be read in different ways. I like that Ms. Quinn put that scene in. It was a brave move on her part. And there is enough ambiguity there to wonder if there was some culpability on Daphne's part. And it turns around some of those ever-present outcries we often get about sexual dynamics in romance.<br /><br />I liked that Simon had his so-called 'flaw'. I don't tend to care for perfect characters, because I don't enjoy rooting for them nearly so much as the flawed/less-than perfect ones. I loved that Daphne accepted that about him, and thought he was wonderful for overcoming the obstacles he faced, and that she thought he was brilliant. She loved him so much, enough to fight for him, and she did many times. In fact, I'd call Daphne the Knight in Shining Armor of this book. Go, Daphne!<br /><br />What was underwhelming about this book? <br /><br />Well, I thought some of the humor aspects were a bit off. I couldn't find the balance between humor and angst. On the plus side, I did like the family dynamics, and the humor they brought to the situation. Those were some of my favorite humorous moments. I liked very much that Daphne's family were useful weapons in her arsenal to win her fair prince. Simon had never felt the loving bonds of family. He was captivated by the Bridgerton family dynamics, good and bad. <br /><br />I must say that Anthony annoyed the crap out of me. He was a bit of a hypocrit. I think that he forgot that Simon was a man he respected, and that he cared about his best friend. When he saw that Simon and Daphne had an attraction to each other, Simon became his enemy. He refused to believe that Simon could be honorable. I know what you're saying. I realize that Anthony took his responsiblity to protect his sister seriously. But, if Simon could look at the situation from Anthony's vantage point, I would hope that Anthony would try to do the same. I didn't see him doing that. I do have to say that I really admired how well Daphne stood up to her over-protective brothers, especially when they tried to interfere in her marriage. She put her foot down, and she needed to, or that wouldn't even stop, for as long as she was married. <br /><br /> The other thing that bothered me about this book was that at times, it seemed to lapse into a modern voice. I know I shouldn't be so picky, but that's a rather large pet peeve of mine. However, I do have to say that for the most part, Ms. Quinn does the Regency period very well.<br /><br />I thought this was a good book, and probably my second favorite novel by Julia Quinn, after To Sir Phillip with Love. I don't go for the lighter Regencies that much, but this had enough angst in it to keep me pretty happy. Although I read it for a challenge, and to get it off my tbr pile, where it had been languishing for several years, I ended up reading it very quickly, and I enjoyed it very much.<br /><br />Overall rating: <b>4.25/5.0 stars</b>.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13919136445461053127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8922389067305904646"><i>Re-read/listened to the audiobook version Oct'2018</i>: <br/><br/>5 stars (with some quibbles) - Historical Romance<br/><br/>The audiobook narrator was great, and overall, it's still a 5-star read for me. But I will say, I didn't like or agree with the heroine's actions. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Daphne took advantage of Simon when he was drunk and aroused and kept him from pulling out in attempt to try and get pregnant despite his strong objections to impregnating her and having children. Consent goes both ways, and she clearly </span></span>
  <span id="freeText8922389067305904646" style="display:none"><i>Re-read/listened to the audiobook version Oct'2018</i>: <br /><br />5 stars (with some quibbles) - Historical Romance<br /><br />The audiobook narrator was great, and overall, it's still a 5-star read for me. But I will say, I didn't like or agree with the heroine's actions. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Daphne took advantage of Simon when he was drunk and aroused and kept him from pulling out in attempt to try and get pregnant despite his strong objections to impregnating her and having children. Consent goes both ways, and she clearly did not have his and manipulated the situation.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>Daphne meant well and was trying to help Simon and things eventually worked out, but the drama between them felt manufactured at times. <br /><br /><br /><i>Original Review from Sept'2010</i>:<br /><br />5 stars – Historical/Regency Romance<br /><br />My introduction to author Julia Quinn was with the books <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6012471.The_Lost_Duke_of_Wyndham__Two_Dukes_of_Wyndham___1_" title="The Lost Duke of Wyndham (Two Dukes of Wyndham, #1) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lost Duke of Wyndham</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2881565.Mr__Cavendish__I_Presume__Two_Dukes_of_Wyndham___2_" title="Mr. Cavendish, I Presume (Two Dukes of Wyndham, #2) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Mr. Cavendish, I Presume</a>, and I wasn’t at all impressed and found them really boring. Several GR friends told me they aren’t her best books or indicative of her other works and that I should give her popular <i>Bridgertons</i> series a chance. I’ve had several of JQ’s books on my TBR shelf for quite a while now, and after mourning the end of two of my favorite HR series, Lisa Kleypas’s beloved <i>Hathaways</i> and Gaelen Foley’s <i>Knight Miscellany</i>, I was looking for another series centered around a family.<br /><br />After hearing such great things about this series from so many trusted GR friends (and also knowing that several of them are on AAR’s Top 100 Romances of 2007 list), I decided to finally read the first book in the <i>Bridgertons</i> series, <b>The Duke and I</b>. And boy oh boy am I ever so glad that I did because it was absolutely <i>delightful</i>!<br /><br />I was worried that it might be a little bit too light and fluffy for my taste; and although there are several humorous moments (I can easily see why JQ is famous for her clever wit!), there are also deeper, emotional elements to the story as well. I loved steadfast, spitfire Daphne and gruff, tormented Simon, and they made such a fun, sweet, endearing couple. They had some wacky and serious obstacles to overcome to be together, but in the end, their HEA left a big ole happy smile on my face. <br /><br />I didn’t feel as strong of a connection to the characters or experience the same lust and love for the hero as I do with every Lisa Kleypas book, and I would have liked a bit (okay, a lot) more steam in the love scenes. But it was still a highly enjoyable, thoroughly romantic story, and I’m looking forward to reading more <i>Bridgertons</i>! 5 stars!</span>

Please marry me, Jane.<br/><br/>Jane: Only if you understand that I cannot have children because I know how badly you want them.<br/> <br/>John: I understand.<br/><br/>Jane: Okay. I’ll marry you.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>A few weeks later...</b>
</i><br/>John: Why do you have birth control pills?<br/><br/>Jane: To prevent pregnancy.<br/><br/>John: I thoug</span>
  <span id="freeText5446609990340978769" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Once upon a time in a make believe world...</b>
</i><br />Jane: I love you, but I can’t marry you. I can’t have children and I want you to be happy. <br /><br />John: We were seen kissing. If we don’t marry, they shall literally burn you at the stake. Please marry me, Jane.<br /><br />Jane: Only if you understand that I cannot have children because I know how badly you want them.<br /> <br />John: I understand.<br /><br />Jane: Okay. I’ll marry you.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>A few weeks later...</b>
</i><br />John: Why do you have birth control pills?<br /><br />Jane: To prevent pregnancy.<br /><br />John: I thought you couldn’t have kids.<br /><br />Jane: Something horrific happened in my childhood. It scarred me for life and I will not have children.<br /><br />John: You lied to me.<br /> <br />Jane: I’ve been in therapy and on antidepressants for 15 years to deal with my childhood. I’m not having children. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>Two months later...</b>
</i><br />Jane: *Screaming* I’m pregnant. How did this happen? When I was on antibiotics you wore condoms.<br /><br />John: I poked holes in them because I want a child<br />********************************************<br /><br />My Dear GR Friends, how does this make you feel? How on earth can this guy take advantage of a woman like this? It’s her body and stuff, right? He needs to respect her wishes?<br /><br />This is kind of what happens in The Duke and I, but it’s the female who wants kids. We sometimes forget that men have rights too. Men are allowed to say NO and women need to respect that. <br /><br />This book was really good up until Daphne disrespected Simon’s wishes and didn’t even have the decency to apologize. Then she was shocked when he left. She also allowed her family to think he was mistreating her.<br /><br />I will probably continue with the series because the Bridgerton brood is interesting, but I need a break first. I didn't like what Daphne did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5446609990340978769" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2074382737" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="NMmomof4" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24665574-nmmomof4"><img alt="NMmomof4" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515474309p2/24665574.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2074382737?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="NMmomof4" class="user" itemprop="url" name="NMmomof4" href="/user/show/24665574-nmmomof4">NMmomof4</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24665574-nmmomof4?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>,
