              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24665574-nmmomof4?shelf=contract-or-marriage-of-convenience">contract-or-marriage-of-convenience</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24665574-nmmomof4?shelf=hr">hr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24665574-nmmomof4?shelf=safe">safe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24665574-nmmomof4?shelf=separation-without-other-partners">separation-without-other-partners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24665574-nmmomof4?shelf=tears">tears</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24665574-nmmomof4?shelf=famous-wealthy-popular">famous-wealthy-popular</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24665574-nmmomof4?shelf=safe-with-exception">safe-with-exception</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2074382737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer74011053691316631"><b> 3 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>Overall Opinion: </b> This was an enjoyable read. I did, however, have some major issues with Daphne's behavior towards the end that causes their separation <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ She seduces him when he is asleep and really drunk, she is on top, and she forces her body down on him to take his completion-- all even though they had been fighting because the H felt strongly that he didn't want children because of his past. To me, this whole scene is borderline rape! I get that he was into it when the</span></span>
  <span id="freeText74011053691316631" style="display:none"><b> 3 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>Overall Opinion: </b> This was an enjoyable read. I did, however, have some major issues with Daphne's behavior towards the end that causes their separation <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ She seduces him when he is asleep and really drunk, she is on top, and she forces her body down on him to take his completion-- all even though they had been fighting because the H felt strongly that he didn't want children because of his past. To me, this whole scene is borderline rape! I get that he was into it when they were in the act, but he was not at all in the right mindset and he didn't want to come in her, and he even made that blatantly obvious all the previous times they had made love!!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I felt like if the roles were reversed, readers would be upset at the H doing something like this! I understand her desperation, but it was wrong. It all worked out it the end for her, but I personally never fully recovered. I enjoyed their banter, overall relationship, and the H! It's just a bummer that that one scene caused me to struggle with an otherwise enjoyable book 😕🤷🏻‍♀️<br /><br /><b>Brief Summary of the Storyline: </b> This is Daphne and Simon's story. Simon had a sad upbringing, and he returns to London only when his father dies to take on the role as the new Duke of Hastings. He meets with his friend from college, Anthony, who happens to be Daphne's older brother. Daphne is out in society and has struggled with her options so far. After forming a friendship, Simon proposes that they both use one another to help with the pains of being in the market for marriage and Daphne agrees. There are some funny moments, some sad and sweet scenes, and a few sexy times...and they get a HEA ending.<br /><br /><b>POV:</b> This alternated between focusing mainly on Daphne and Simon in 3rd person narrative.<br /><br /><b>Overall Pace of Story: </b> Good, I never skimmed and I thought it flowed well.<br /><br /><b>Instalove:</b> No. They become friends first then develop stronger feelings.<br /><br /><b>H rating:</b> 4.5 stars. Simon. I really liked him! He was damaged, stubborn, and even bitter -- but I got it, and his past broke my heart!<br /><br /><b>h rating:</b> 2.5 stars. Daphne. I really liked her until a particular scene at the end where I couldn't believe her behavior!<br /><br /><b>Sadness level: </b>Low/moderate. I never needed any tissues, but I did shed a few tears.<br /><br /><b>Push/Pull:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The H pushes away, but I'd say that they both pursue the relationship at times. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Heat level:</b> Good. They have some good tension, chemistry, and scenes -- but not so much it takes away from the story.<br /><br /><b>Descriptive sex:</b> Yes<br /><br /><b>OW/OM drama:</b> No<br /><br /><b>Sex scene with OW or OM:</b> No<br /><br /><b>Cheating: </b> No<br /><br /><b>Separation:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They are separated for ~2 months (after they're married and not a legal separation), but there was no mention or suggestion of other partners during this time.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Possible Triggers: </b>Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The H has a speech impediment (on page), child emotional abuse/neglect (H's dad - mostly off page), and virgin h.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Closure: </b> This edition that I read even had a second epilogue! So, lots of closure and a HEA! <br /><br /><b>Safety:</b> This one should be either <u>Safe</u> or <u>Safe with exception </u> for most safety gang readers depending on personal preferences.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have cheating<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have a descriptive sex scene with OW/OM<br />- <b> Does</b> have the H pushing the h away<br />- <b> Does</b> have a separation between the h and H<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have abuse by mcs (unless you count the scene described in my first spoiler tag)<br />- <b>Does </b> have a HEA ending <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25322247-the-duke-and-i">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3031955114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6875222497390694786">The Duke and I is my second foray into historical romance and I can definitely say that I've found a new favorite genre. It's really exciting to go into books and not be able to predict anything since I'm not as familiar with the tropes or story structures of the genre. I found myself enchanted by the lovable Bridgerton family and I cannot wait to devour this entire series and then watch the upcoming Netflix adaptation! The one thing I will say is that I was loving this book, and I was leaning t</span>
  <span id="freeText6875222497390694786" style="display:none">The Duke and I is my second foray into historical romance and I can definitely say that I've found a new favorite genre. It's really exciting to go into books and not be able to predict anything since I'm not as familiar with the tropes or story structures of the genre. I found myself enchanted by the lovable Bridgerton family and I cannot wait to devour this entire series and then watch the upcoming Netflix adaptation! The one thing I will say is that I was loving this book, and I was leaning toward 5 stars until something very not okay happened. Like, VERY VERY not okay. Fortunately, it didn't derail my previous enjoyment up until that point nor did it ruin the whole book for me, but I can definitely understand why it would for others. I've heard that the series keeps getting better from here so I am glad I read book one and got to meet all of the Bridgertons at the very beginning of their story. There was a lot more humor than I was expecting and the inclusion of Lady Whistledown's society column gave the book a kind of historical Gossip Girl feeling. I already have book two checked out and ready to read!</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1146600177965417114">One of my 2020 reading goals was more reading and less reviewing. That being said, The Duke and I was a scrumptious bite of historical romance and I was 100% along for the ride. Angsty, with a hero who is a jerk (but actually not). Since the series will be coming soon, you need to make this book a reading priority asap!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer998815998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12506000244181079537">Some spoilers ahead, so consider yourself forewarned.<br/><br/>Oh where to begin...<br/><br/>I suppose the beginning was not that bad. The characters were a little bit flat, but it was interesting enough. Cheesy, but readable.<br/>The part when they kiss for the first time was hilarious. I'm not really sure if it was intended, but still.<br/><br/>But then, as Daphne became increasingly pathetic with every chapter, and Simon became an even bigger asshole, the book was quickly turning from readable to insufferable. <br/><br/>And then it culm</span>
  <span id="freeText12506000244181079537" style="display:none">Some spoilers ahead, so consider yourself forewarned.<br /><br />Oh where to begin...<br /><br />I suppose the beginning was not that bad. The characters were a little bit flat, but it was interesting enough. Cheesy, but readable.<br />The part when they kiss for the first time was hilarious. I'm not really sure if it was intended, but still.<br /><br />But then, as Daphne became increasingly pathetic with every chapter, and Simon became an even bigger asshole, the book was quickly turning from readable to insufferable. <br /><br />And then it culminated.<br /><br />So Daphne's biggest wish in life is to marry and have children. I understand that women in the past were brought up with only that purpose, but in many HR novels, while the heroines do want marriage, they are also more than just that. The defining feature of Daphne's character is her wish to marry and have children. Like she doesn't exist beyond that. <br />While I personally, don't feel like Daphne, I would respect her dreams if she had <b>any other</b> aspirations in life. Anything at all.<br /><br />So Daphne, limited twit that she is, decides to take advantage of her drunk and sleeping husband, even though the night before they had a HUUUGE fight about how Simon doesn't want to be a father.<br />And I can't even. How is that okay?! Of course he would run away!! The man was sleeping, he was not a consenting adult in that. That scene made my blood boil.<br />It's considered ungentlemanly and dishonorable when a man takes advantage of drunk woman, but when a woman does it, it's okay? <br />The worst thing is, Simon felt betrayed and Daphne didn't even understand that what she did was terribly wrong <b>like what the fuck?!?!?!?!?!?!?!?</b> Girl, you were not that sheltered. <br /><br />So anyway, after that scene I lost any interest I had left for this book and for the characters. <br />But the book has pretty high ratings here on GR, so it seems that a lot of people <s>don't mind rape if it's done by the female character</s> liked it. Read and decide for yourself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12506000244181079537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText14948648500975991894" style="display:none">So this book went from 4 stars to a 2 stars...<br><br>Where to begin....<br><br>OH THERE ARE MANY SPOILERS IN THIS RANT..ERM, I MEAN REVIEW...<br><br>I really enjoyed this beginning of this book. I liked Simon and I seriously felt for him. He had a horrible father who ignored his existence because of he stuttered... Poor, poor Simon...<br><br>Then we have the little chit who to be known as our heroine....her name is Daphne... we will not dwell on her attributes since she was a poor excuse for a female character. Instead, we will spend time on her dumb actions in this book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453345210ra/17814405.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>K....so I liked her a bit in the beginning before her character was revealed. She was fresh and unique. She had 3 (or was it 4?) older brothers from which she learnt the ways of men and rakes...well according to her....She claimed to be all knowledgeable when it came to the opposite sex...but she was actually a complete dimwit.<br><br>Anyways....moving on...<br><br>So Simon must make the decision if he wanted to marry her or die by the hands of her brother, Anthony. <br><br>He chooses the death option...<br><br>Only nope, DING, DING, DING! You got it, Daphne comes in between the duel and practically forces him to marry her because her reputation was ruined... I get it, she did in fact 'love' him but that's besides the point that he NEVER wanted to marry...but I decided to let this go for I knew he would fall in love with her...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459215974ra/18582733.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Then here comes the big whammy I will NEVER FORGIVE THIS POOR EXCUSE OF A WOMAN FOR...<br><br>Simon NEVER EVER wanted kids because of his bad experiences and he never wanted his father to 'win'. He tells Daphne he CAN'T have children not that he WON'T, she finds out...blahhh, blahh, blaaahhh.....<br><br>The guy comes home drunk one night and she comes up with this "brilliant" idea to have sex with him while he's still drunk. So she arouses him in his sleep and then hops on him. Once he comes to his senses and still is a little bit drowsy from the alcohol, he tries to push her off but he couldn't since she held on with all her strength. So he finished inside her which was against his wishes. <br><br>I WILL NEVER FORGIVE HER BECAUSE SHE BASICALLY RAPES SIMON AND THEN DOESN'T THINK SHE DID ANYTHING WRONG...She never learnt that she made such a horrible mistake. She thought of only herself and her dreams of wanting a baby. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459215870ra/18582728.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What in the actual heck..???...<br><br>She is such a big manipulator that I can't even...form coherent thoughts about her...I feel like I'l go on a swearing rampage ....<br><br>I know this is more a rant than review but I needed to get it all out there.... I will read the second one because it was recommended to me by a good friend, plus, I did enjoy the writing just not the female character.<br><br><br></span>

<div id="review_372431154" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/372431154" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/372431154?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer372431154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3599474373519034419"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Save your pathetic words," Anthony spat. "I'll see you at dawn."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Please let there be a duel. Pleeeeaaasssse let there be a duel.</i><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380384607i/743172.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>One sec, flipping the page. *pause* Damn...no duel.</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I've always known that I wasn't the sort of woman men dream of, but I never thought anyone would prefer death to marriage with me."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>3.5 stars. I would have definitely gone for a solid 4 star had there been a duel. What a missed opportunity that was! There are more brothers in this family; it woul</span>
  <span id="freeText3599474373519034419" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Save your pathetic words," Anthony spat. "I'll see you at dawn."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>Please let there be a duel. Pleeeeaaasssse let there be a duel.</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380384607i/743172.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>One sec, flipping the page. *pause* Damn...no duel.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I've always known that I wasn't the sort of woman men dream of, but I never thought anyone would prefer death to marriage with me."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>3.5 stars. I would have definitely gone for a solid 4 star had there been a duel. What a missed opportunity that was! There are more brothers in this family; it wouldn't have been a big deal to off one of them.<br><br>So, I am no longer a Quinn virgin. The seduction is complete. Gonna take a sec and stub out this "we made it official" cigarette so I can write my review.<br><br><b>Summary in a sentence :</b> A duke who was abused and shunned in his childhood because of a speech impediment grows up to be a handsome young man that pushes away the one woman who sees him for more than what his father made him out to be.<br><br><b>Truth be told, I wasn't a fan of the first half of this book.</b> The banter was lackluster, the sexual tension was almost nonexistent, and not a whole lot really happened.<br><br><b>Who knew that a failed duel scene would be the turning point of the story?</b> I have <i>no</i> idea what happened, but once Daphne rode in on her horse, ready to throw herself in the way if necessary in order to stop her brother and the man she loved from shooting themselves, it was as if life had suddenly been breathed into the dying tale. From there on out, it became fun. All of a sudden, Daphne and Simon were actually worth reading about.<br><br><b>I liked seeing a few reminders of other series I've enjoyed in the past</b>. <i>The Bridgertons</i> came along before series like <i>The Hathaways</i> and <i>The Luxe</i> but since I read the latter 2 series beforehand, I had a smile on my face when I noticed the "gossip column" segments as chapter headers (Luxe), then later couldn't help but get excited over the possibilities of seeing what's to come in the future for the siblings of the main character (Hathaways). I especially can't wait for Colin's story. He sounds like the fun and careless rake : <i>Colin's one-shoulder shrug matched his lopsided smile to perfection.</i> The mother is also a riot. Her dialogue in the scene where she's explaining to her daughter what happens on the wedding night was priceless.<br><br><b>Addressing the somewhat controversial scene...</b> Okay, so I'd seen mention of a scene in this book which might raise an eyebrow for some people. I understand that had the roles been reversed, it would have been an extremely difficult scene to read. I don't mean to fall into the category of double standards because I do agree that the manipulation was extremely wrong. It just didn't anger me the way it did others. She made a bad choice in the moment and did end up having to pay for it to some extent, so at least she was partially held responsible for her actions. <br><br><b>Sexy time was eventually sexy.</b> The steam factor wasn't off the charts and it took a while before I even felt the heat between this couple but it got there at some point.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>As his hands moved to his trousers, he saw that she was pulling the bedsheets over her. "Don't," he said, barely recognizing his own voice. Her eyes met his and he said, "I'll be your blanket."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Overall, this was a nice read. Not my favorite historical romance, but still an endearing love story when everything came together.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Simon, she pleaded, "save me."<br><br>And he was lost.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3599474373519034419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holly" href="/user/show/7383561-holly">Holly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062911414" href="/book/show/41824564-the-duke-and-i">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7383561-holly?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7383561-holly?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7383561-holly?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3620284749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer873260068563611677">2.5 stars<br/><br/><b>How in the world are they going to turn this into a Netflix series?!</b> It's coming out on Netflix on Christmas Day and is produced by THE Shonda Rhimes, but seriously I have no idea how they are going to pull it off because there are some SERIOUSLY QUESTIONABLE things going on in this book. It starts off great - I loved the introduction to the large Bridgerton family, they felt like such a real family with different personalities but lots of love and exasperation between them all, especia</span>
  <span id="freeText873260068563611677" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br /><br /><b>How in the world are they going to turn this into a Netflix series?!</b> It's coming out on Netflix on Christmas Day and is produced by THE Shonda Rhimes, but seriously I have no idea how they are going to pull it off because there are some SERIOUSLY QUESTIONABLE things going on in this book. It starts off great - I loved the introduction to the large Bridgerton family, they felt like such a real family with different personalities but lots of love and exasperation between them all, especially between the oldest four siblings. I even initially enjoyed the romance between the MCs, Daphne and Simon. Their plan to pretend a courtship in order to make Daphne appear more desirable to other men and to protect Simon from having to deal with banal young women and their pushy mothers, is carried off well enough. But then we get to a scene where they are together in a garden and from there the book starts to go down in my esteem. And then we get to a drunken moment and it basically plummets to the point of no return. How they are going to represent that scene in particular on Netflix, I am VERY curious about. Because seriously, it's messed up. We shall see!</span>
  <a data-text-id="873260068563611677" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25322247-the-duke-and-i">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68070948-elena-c?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68070948-elena-c?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68070948-elena-c?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2338231969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11291092385620274829">Julia Quinn writes delightfully funny banters.<br/><br/>Julia Quinn has an obvious knack for romantic comedy.<br/><br/>Julia Quinn can turn the simple act of taking a glove off into something sensual.<br/><br/><b>Julia Quinn is utterly confused about what constitutes consent and what doesn't</b>.<br/><br/>*spoilers ahead*<br/><br/>Just imagine: you've repeatedly stated that you do not want to have kids. You're taking every possible measure to ensure you don't end up pregnant. But hey, your partner knows best. So the day you have way too much to drink </span>
  <span id="freeText11291092385620274829" style="display:none">Julia Quinn writes delightfully funny banters.<br /><br />Julia Quinn has an obvious knack for romantic comedy.<br /><br />Julia Quinn can turn the simple act of taking a glove off into something sensual.<br /><br /><b>Julia Quinn is utterly confused about what constitutes consent and what doesn't</b>.<br /><br />*spoilers ahead*<br /><br />Just imagine: you've repeatedly stated that you do not want to have kids. You're taking every possible measure to ensure you don't end up pregnant. But hey, your partner knows best. So the day you have way too much to drink and go to bed wasted, he has unprotected sex with you in hope to knock you up - because yes, he might have said he was okay with you not wanting a family, but... come on, seriously?! Once you're with child, you'll surely see reason. His reason, that is.<br /><br />Real charming, isn't it? Now swap the gender of the protagonists of this sweet little romance: does the fact that it was a man and not a woman who was taken advantage of change anything? If you think it doesn't, then probably you'd better stay clear of <b>The Duke and I</b>.<br /><br /><b>The book was funny and adorable until it wasn't</b>. I was ecstatic when Daphne confronted Simon about his stupid and offensive ploy to avoid getting her pregnant: he deliberately misled her into thinking he couldn't have children - when, in fact, he simply didn't want to; and he did so taking advantage of his wife's obvious (and unavoidable, given the times) ignorance of sex. Not cool. And the whole reason behind him not wanting kids was pretty asinine, really. But still. You talk to him. You try to understand what brought him to such a drastic decision and make him understand your needs and hopes for the future. You try to be patient - after all it's been what, two weeks since the marriage? <br /><br />Or, you know, you can always take advantage of the drunk moron who passed out in your bed. There. All done!<br /><br />The fact that neither Daphne nor Simon - or Quinn herself, obviously - seemed to think that anything much was wrong with this scenario had me alternately outraged and seriously confused. I mean - pardon my French here - but: <i>
  <b>what the actual fuck</b>
</i>? Is it just me? I re-read that awful passage three times and there's just no way to make it right, no matter how <i>blasé</i> Daphne and Simon are about it. Whatever, guys: if you're happy... <br /><br />... still, what a way to wreck an otherwise perfectly lovely romance.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11291092385620274829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7389648638395762531"><b>2.75</b><br/><br/><i>OH BOI</i><br/><br/>sooo I finished this book <b>(I FINALLY FINISHED A BOOK OMG I CAN READ AGAIN)</b> and I have like a <b>GAZILLION</b> thoughts about it. I have no idea how the <i>hell</i> I'm going to rate this. My mind is <b>SWIRLING LIKE A FREAKING TORNADO</b> with opinions on this, and I need a minute to put them in order so I can try to write a somewhat <i>coherent</i> review.<br/><br/><b>EDIT:</b> So I come from the future to say that I actually enjoyed this book a lot, uuuntil the protagonist did something <b>extremely fucked up</b> and problematic towar</span>
  <span id="freeText7389648638395762531" style="display:none"><b>2.75</b><br /><br /><i>OH BOI</i><br /><br />sooo I finished this book <b>(I FINALLY FINISHED A BOOK OMG I CAN READ AGAIN)</b> and I have like a <b>GAZILLION</b> thoughts about it. I have no idea how the <i>hell</i> I'm going to rate this. My mind is <b>SWIRLING LIKE A FREAKING TORNADO</b> with opinions on this, and I need a minute to put them in order so I can try to write a somewhat <i>coherent</i> review.<br /><br /><b>EDIT:</b> So I come from the future to say that I actually enjoyed this book a lot, uuuntil the protagonist did something <b>extremely fucked up</b> and problematic towards the end, which left me <i>shooketh</i> because when I decided to <b>give historical romance a chance</b> I always thought that if someone was going to <i>screw up</i> it would be the <i>male romantic interest</i> (bc let's be honest that's usually the case), but nope. I actually felt <i>bad</i> for him, because if the roles were reversed he would get a lot of shit because of that, and <i>rightfully so,</i> but since she's a woman the author made it seem as if it's like... okay?<br /><br />Up until that point I was surprisingly <b>having a great time</b> with this novel, which is the ONLY reason my rating didn't drop to the <i>floor.</i> I might give the next book in the series a chance because it has a different protagonist, but now I'm a bit concerned with the author choices. We'll see what happens.<br /><br />-------------------------------------------<br /><br /><b>PREREVIEW</b><br /><br />Ok I've been trying to come out of the <i>Great Reading Slump of 2019</i> (haven't read a book in 3 months 😵) and I've been particularly struggling to figure out what to read.<br /><br />I was never much for romance as a genre, especially not historical romance books. Idk, I don’t find very captivating to read about the less than ideal way women were gererally treated back then and I'm very picky when it comes to the development of relationships.<br /><br />That said, I know Julia Quinn's books are quite popular, and since there's a netflix series coming out on the Bridgertons (and I heard people discussing the casting choices) I was like "oh what the hell, I'll give this a shot".<br /><br />This is completely out of my comfort zone, so let's hope I can make it through.</span>

Daphne and Simon were an attractive couple, the three brothers were hilarious and the Bridgerton family as a whole were charming. There was lots of humorous banter and some real laugh aloud moments. <div id="review_58107489" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer58107489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9933284468128730526"><i>Ah my Gentle Reader, this Reviewer is pleased to report, that one cannot argue against; I loved this book.</i><br/><br/> It was fun to read about Simon and Daphne finding each other through angry brothers, duels, crazy marriage mind mamas and a few misunderstandings along the way. The banter between the was laugh out loud funny as were some of the arguments .<br/> <br/> Simon was a great hero, dealing with his past and the treatment his father dealt him at such an early age, making it his goal in life to prove his fath</span>
  <span id="freeText9933284468128730526" style="display:none"><i>Ah my Gentle Reader, this Reviewer is pleased to report, that one cannot argue against; I loved this book.</i><br /><br /> It was fun to read about Simon and Daphne finding each other through angry brothers, duels, crazy marriage mind mamas and a few misunderstandings along the way. The banter between the was laugh out loud funny as were some of the arguments .<br /> <br /> Simon was a great hero, dealing with his past and the treatment his father dealt him at such an early age, making it his goal in life to prove his father wrong over and over again. Not seeing the fact that while proving his dead father wrong was just proving his father was right and making him unhappy in the process. <br /> Daphne was a strong lead for Simon and a strong lady (no really, she got one hellva punch!) While not having the harsh treatment that Simon did, she does have her own battles to fight between her family and Simon. Yet, she always manages to keep a happy and thoughtful outlook on life and look at things on the bright side of life. <br /> Together both make a wonderful and funny couple whom bring out the best in each other even with crazy family members around them trying to rule them over.<br /> <br /> I really adore Daphne family, her brothers were a hoot but her Mom was the best, bringing all her sons to order with a few choice words or a yank of a ear. And a cute running mystery of who the infamous Ms. Whistledown truly is. <br /><br /> Overall: a great and fun read with a lots of laughs and a lot of love!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9933284468128730526" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7hTAW/j4DS2rS5e7k3UxpDr0QjSLhmhf1hLIZZ41DpsO9PBLPSfJbqKr1Q27Mm+uE5ZQgfAKDa+WpveNc1CdAg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NUDUzPzHNLjCT0HKnQ+REoeoTAoGryqnY09eekM+vbjVoOTcORjw+8uvA3y1SM8Yrspev30jT1cj+2GSrlsuIQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7753905585732684444">#1 New York Times bestselling author Julia Quinn loves to dispel the myth that smart women don't read (or write) romance, and and if you watch reruns of the game show The Weakest Link you might just catch her winning the $79,000 jackpot. She displayed a decided lack of knowledge about baseball, country music, and plush toys, but she is proud to say that she aced all things British and literary, an</span>
  <span id="freeText7753905585732684444" style="display:none">#1 New York Times bestselling author Julia Quinn loves to dispel the myth that smart women don't read (or write) romance, and and if you watch reruns of the game show The Weakest Link you might just catch her winning the $79,000 jackpot. She displayed a decided lack of knowledge about baseball, country music, and plush toys, but she is proud to say that she aced all things British and literary, answered all of her history and geography questions correctly, and knew that there was a Da Vinci long before there was a code.<br /><br />A graduate of Harvard and Radcliffe Colleges, Ms. Quinn is one of only sixteen members of Romance Writers of America’s Hall of Fame. Her books have been translated into 32 languages, and she lives with her family in the Pacific Northwest.<br /><br />The Bridgertons, her popular series of historical romance, is currently in production by Shondaland as a Netflix original series starring Julie Andrews, Phoebe Dynevor, and Rége-Jean Page.</span>
